<div id="review_124825749" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124825749" />
    <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog"><img alt="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352609417p2/2489554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124825749?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog">Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Nalini Singh fans and paranormal romance fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=keep-a-spare-pair-of-knickers">keep-a-spare-pair-of-knickers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=my-hottie-harem">my-hottie-harem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=king-of-the-harem">king-of-the-harem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=author-nalini-singh">author-nalini-singh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=books-i-go-rabid-over">books-i-go-rabid-over</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124825749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10806411918248821047"><i>Hostage to Pleasure</i> is the fifth book in the Psy-Changeling series and Dorian has been one of my favourite DarkRiver sentinels from the very start! <br/><br/>He’s latent, which means he can’t shift and although many see it as a disadvantage, <b>Dorian</b> doesn’t let that hinder his determination and protectiveness over Pack. He makes up for it with his sniper abilities and sharp mind. I loved his charm in <i> Mine to Possess</i> so I was very excited to read his story. Instead, Dorian was very angry and tense for most</span>
  <span id="freeText10806411918248821047" style="display:none"><i>Hostage to Pleasure</i> is the fifth book in the Psy-Changeling series and Dorian has been one of my favourite DarkRiver sentinels from the very start! <br /><br />He’s latent, which means he can’t shift and although many see it as a disadvantage, <b>Dorian</b> doesn’t let that hinder his determination and protectiveness over Pack. He makes up for it with his sniper abilities and sharp mind. I loved his charm in <i> Mine to Possess</i> so I was very excited to read his story. Instead, Dorian was very angry and tense for most of his book. The reason is understandable since his lost his baby sister, Kylie to one of the Psy. But I found myself wishing there was more of that charm towards Aleine. We see it, but it’s towards Mercy and a little bit with Tally as well. I would have loved to see the sparks fly with a Psy.<br /><br /><b>Aleine</b> is an M-Psy and I see her differently than Sascha and Faith. She already showed signs of feelings and emotions so I thought her transition in breaking Silence would be quicker. I loved her moments with her son, Keenan! They were so sweet! <b>Keenan</b> saying he wanted to marry Noor was adorable! I am a total sucker for motherly moments like that!<br /><br /><b>Amara</b>, Ashaya’s twin sister, annoyed from the very beginning. I saw her as a threat to Dorian and Shaya, so even though she wasn’t as ruthless and psycho as the other killers we see in the previous books, I just couldn’t find myself liking her all that much. She was scary possessive of her twin sister and every time she said “She’s mine,” I wanted to bitch slap her. Reading about what she did to Shaya as an “experiment” also pissed me off. <br /><br /><b>Mercy’s</b> book is next! And I loved the friendly banter between Dorian and Merce! I cannot wait to read her book! Is it bad to say that I’m happy that the main characters are not Psy? I can’t seem to love them as much as the DarkRiver and SnowDancer packs. They are just too unemotional for me!<br /><br />Also, I just wanted to say that I love how Singh incorporates interracial couplings in her books! She is one of the authors who doesn’t see race as a boundary and uses it enhance her books is an amazing way! Singh, you have officially become one of my favourite authors!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10806411918248821047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1404461083" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1404461083?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=werewolves-and-other-furry-shifters">werewolves-and-other-furry-shifters</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1404461083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1227693176268771447">Oooooh, I've been waiting for this book because Dorian has been one of my favorite males in this series. (Hawke is number one). Let's see, he has blonde hair, blue eyes, and is beautiful. I wonder why that attracts my attention...?? <br/><br/>I know what you all are thinking. Oh, brother, here goes Jilly on another one of her "Chris Hemsworth is the perfect specimen of man" tangents. Gee, give me a break! There are plenty of other gorgeous blonde men out there that are (almost) as beautiful. I'm not that </span>
  <span id="freeText1227693176268771447" style="display:none">Oooooh, I've been waiting for this book because Dorian has been one of my favorite males in this series. (Hawke is number one). Let's see, he has blonde hair, blue eyes, and is beautiful. I wonder why that attracts my attention...?? <br><br>I know what you all are thinking. Oh, brother, here goes Jilly on another one of her "Chris Hemsworth is the perfect specimen of man" tangents. Gee, give me a break! There are plenty of other gorgeous blonde men out there that are (almost) as beautiful. I'm not that obsessed. (I totally am). So, to show my flexibility in this, I will use another blonde man as a visual aid. This is all in the name of science, of course.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443682429i/16395506._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>he's Hemsworth-pretty</i><br><br>So, that's Dorian. His love interest in this book is Shaya, a psy scientist, and brilliant. She looks like this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443682429i/16395507._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Shaya has a son and a twin sister. Her twin is a sociopath and is planning on killing her son, so Shaya made a deal with Dorian in a previous book that she would help the pack rescue two other kids if he would retrieve her son when she asked. Dorian has a soft-spot for kids and immediately falls in love with the kid.<br><br>An Alpha male bonding with a cute 4-yr old boy? How precious is that? Cuz, we all know that in real-life getting a guy to even go out on a date with a single mother is like pulling teeth. Only in our book-land can we get the most beautiful guy in the pack to mate with a single mother.<br><br>If we actually thought book-boyfriends would be like real-life men, we would be like these people:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443682429ra/16395508.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443682429ra/16395509.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443682429i/16395510._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Reality isn't pretty!</i><br><br>And, the reality of this book was that I didn't really like Shaya as much as I had hoped. I think I am ready for a female MC with a bit more oomph. The good news is that Mercy's book is next, and she is an awesome character. Bring it on!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16110514937173700404"><b>"The leopard knows."</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428254826i/14395890._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>________________________________________<br/><br/>2nd read - 5 March to 7 March 2013<br/>3rd read - 23 April to 27 April 2014<br/>4th read - 3 April to 5 April 2015<br/>5th read - 2 May to 6 May 2017<br/>_________________________________________<br/><br/>So I have a little bit of a Dorian crush, I love myself an emotionally damaged overachiever, I can't help myself. So on that note I felt it necessary to cast him. <br/><b>Dorian</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398293210i/9396197._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>*If I can find images of what I imagine my two other favourite emotionally damaged men in this s</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16110514937173700404" style="display:none"><b>"The leopard knows."</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428254826i/14395890._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>________________________________________<br><br>2nd read - 5 March to 7 March 2013<br>3rd read - 23 April to 27 April 2014<br>4th read - 3 April to 5 April 2015<br>5th read - 2 May to 6 May 2017<br>_________________________________________<br><br>So I have a little bit of a Dorian crush, I love myself an emotionally damaged overachiever, I can't help myself. So on that note I felt it necessary to cast him. <br><b>Dorian</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398293210i/9396197._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>*If I can find images of what I imagine my two other favourite emotionally damaged men in this series look like when I get to their reviews, I will also cast them but unfortunately I really don't think that there are men who look like <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Hawke and Kaleb <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> in this world.</i><br><br>Anyhoots. So Dorian is delicious and Ashaya is amazing. I loved the development of their relationship, it was intense and emotional. Dorian is so angry he is actually frightening at times but Ashaya is so strong and has been surrounded in the most dangerous of adversaries for so long that she deals with him beautifully. Again we have the predator male pushing and pushing even in situations when I think he knew himself that he should stop. Dorian and Ashaya's relationship starts off with a kind of obsession, we get some insight into this obsession with diary entries from Ashaya and Dorian's POV. From the moment they met (even though they met in unusual circumstances) things seemed to be inevitable. <br><br>The most beautiful part of this story for me was Ashaya and Keenan's relationship, the Psy Net is a cold and scary place but yet a four year old boy was completely aware of his mothers love for him when so many other children the same age in the Net have never experienced love at all. It was really sweet and is testament to how ballsy and kick ass Ashaya really is. Dorian's developing relationship with Keenan was also lovely and watching them all become a family made me all happy in my heart.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397802374ra/9330266.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now the out and out best character in this book had to be Amara. I know she is a sociopath and I really shouldn't like her but I in particular loved how she wound up Ming and just didn't care what the council did to her. She was sooooooo different from any other character that we have come across in this series. Reading her was just a joy. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381339490ra/4727834.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397221655ra/9249178.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We have another group introduced in this book that the Changelings have to worry about. The Human Alliance makes a brief appearance but there is definitely a feeling that there will be more to come from these guys. <br><br>In terms of groupings, we now have:<br><br>The Changelings (primarily DarkRiver and SnowDancer)<br>The Psy Council<br>The Arrows (part of the Psy and Assassins for the council) <br>The Forgotten <br>The Human Alliance <br><br>A lot of people to cause a lot of problems. <br><br>This was a great book, 5 crazy twin sister and yummy sentinel stars.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_88043355" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/88043355" />
    <a title="Beanbag Love" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2598237-beanbag-love"><img alt="Beanbag Love" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249531311p2/2598237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/88043355?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beanbag Love" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beanbag Love" href="/user/show/2598237-beanbag-love">Beanbag Love</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer88043355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1775274485013661945">Nalini Singh drives me a little nuts. Every one of the Psy-Changeling books I've read has made me so frustrated in the first half and then made me love it in the second. I swear, it's at 50% in each book that things pick up.<br/><br/>In Hostage to Pleasure we get the story of two characters we've met in earlier books. Dorian, the latent leopard changeling, has been around since he wanted to rip out Sascha's throat in the first book. Ashaya was introduced in the last book -- Mine to Possess -- although I t</span>
  <span id="freeText1775274485013661945" style="display:none">Nalini Singh drives me a little nuts. Every one of the Psy-Changeling books I've read has made me so frustrated in the first half and then made me love it in the second. I swear, it's at 50% in each book that things pick up.<br /><br />In Hostage to Pleasure we get the story of two characters we've met in earlier books. Dorian, the latent leopard changeling, has been around since he wanted to rip out Sascha's throat in the first book. Ashaya was introduced in the last book -- Mine to Possess -- although I think she might have been referenced in Caressed by Ice.<br /><br />Dorian's a fave. The guy who can't shift, who's all pent up because of his 'disability', his sister's murder and the continuing stress of a war with the Psy. Ashaya is an M-Psy who's been working on the Protocol 1 chip that will create a hive mind among the Psy. Naturally, she's been rogue for a while and finds herself needing to escape. Dorian ends up being her bodyguard which is kind of nice for both of them since they've been obsessing over each other since he threatened to kill her in Mine to Possess. <br /><br />Ashaya's got all kinds of other problems that I won't go into, but, without giving any specifics, these probs were what annoyed me. For fully half of the book we got her POV saying things like: "it wasn't {blank}, it was something far worse". This was said about three different things multiple times. At one point I said "oh give me a break!" out loud and put the book down for the night I was so annoyed. That's not creating suspense, it's creating frustration. <br /><br />Interestingly enough, as soon as some of that actual information started to be shared with the reader the book became very enjoyable. <br /><br />So, having seen that K is working on "Slave to Sensation" and feeling frustrated, I think it's not just me. Keep going, get past that 50% mark and suddenly you've got a heck of a story. Since this was book five, I doubt the template's going to change much. By the last book -- the fourth in the series -- I knew to look forward to that halfway point, knowing I would really get into it by then.<br /><br />There you have it. The second half is five stars. The first half is three stars (at most). A solid four star read by the end.<br /><br />**for those who have read it -- possible spoiler follows**<br /><br />I wanted more from the epilogue. There were reactions beyond that little group that I wanted to read about. I wish I hadn't had to write that sequence in my head, because I think it would have been relevant to the story as a whole. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1775274485013661945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1125631747" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1125631747" />
    <a title="Naomi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20128361-naomi"><img alt="Naomi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418567627p2/20128361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1125631747?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naomi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naomi" href="/user/show/20128361-naomi">Naomi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=tattooed-and-pierced">tattooed-and-pierced</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=alpha-males">alpha-males</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=all-kinds-of-shapeshifters">all-kinds-of-shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=mes-coups-de-coeur">mes-coups-de-coeur</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=big-bad-werewolves">big-bad-werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=nalini-singh">nalini-singh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1125631747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10728068368924070332"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417996723i/12633714.png' width='400' height='250' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Pieces of my heart, Dorian. You're in so many pieces of my heart."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>I am in love with this series. Seriously. I never thought I could love a series that much after having read so many different series but, here it is. I love everything about these books, the universe, the writing style, the characters: all different and interesting, the plot... each book is fascinating and I can barely wait to read the next one. <br/><br/><b>Hostage to Pleasure</b> is Dorian's story and let me tell you, I have been <i>*i</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10728068368924070332" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417996723i/12633714.png" width="400" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Pieces of my heart, Dorian. You're in so many pieces of my heart."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>I am in love with this series. Seriously. I never thought I could love a series that much after having read so many different series but, here it is. I love everything about these books, the universe, the writing style, the characters: all different and interesting, the plot... each book is fascinating and I can barely wait to read the next one. <br><br><b>Hostage to Pleasure</b> is Dorian's story and let me tell you, I have been <i>*impatiently*</i> waiting to read his book. I was not disappointed. It was everything I wanted it to be. <br><br>Dorian intrigued me since the first book, he is such an amazing character. So strong, loyal, latent (he cannot change, he remains human) and yet stronger than some of his pack. He's filled with hurt and revenge. I was skeptical about the heroine at first, she didn't seem very likable in the previous book but I was wrong there too, because I loved Ashaya. Loved her. She is my favorite heroine so far. <br><br>Ashaya is a M-Psy, very smart, strong and filled with love for her son and twin. She surprised me, I did not expect to love her that much and to feel for her that much either. This woman went through so much, she's so tough and selfless. <br><br>The two of them together, it was everything I wanted. Everything. If not better. They were perfect for each other and Nalini is such an amazing writer, she blew me away. Dorian is just so hot, it's not funny. The sex scenes were hot and yes, there aren't a lot of those and we have to wait some time before it finally happens but it was worth it (so worth it, though) and necessary. Nalini knows what she's doing and she's doing it perfectly. <br><br>I don't really know what to say, just that I loved this book and I want more. I especially loved the epilogue, so sweet and emotional. It could've been longer though, it wouldn't have bothered me! <br><br>In <b>Hostage to Pleasure</b> we learn more about certain characters... and I cannot wait to read Kaleb's story because he doesn't seem that good to me. And Mercy's story is next, so excited! I loved the secondary characters as well. Especially little Keenan, so cute.<br><br>The plot was beyond interesting and intriguing, it kept me reading, I had things to do, yet I couldn't stop, I had to know what was going to happen. I really hope the series keeps getting better and better because this book was just perfect.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10728068368924070332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2013-read">2013-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2019-read">2019-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer582978267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18305554984193599295">September 2016 Re-read: I've been a little surprised a couple of times on this re-read, my millionth since first picking up the series, and going into this book I was slightly worried that it was going to come off worse.<br/><br/>When I first read this series I was INCREDIBLY forgiving of almost anything the male characters did. I'm not sure why this is, but I've noticed that it was common for me at that point in my reading-life. In fact, it was pretty common for me up until a couple of years ago. Being a</span>
  <span id="freeText18305554984193599295" style="display:none">September 2016 Re-read: I've been a little surprised a couple of times on this re-read, my millionth since first picking up the series, and going into this book I was slightly worried that it was going to come off worse.<br /><br />When I first read this series I was INCREDIBLY forgiving of almost anything the male characters did. I'm not sure why this is, but I've noticed that it was common for me at that point in my reading-life. In fact, it was pretty common for me up until a couple of years ago. Being a woman, I thought I'd always very strongly supported women. And I did (and do) in real life. But I've come to realize that I was being unfair in my judgments of characters in the books I read. Women were judged more harshly, men were more easily forgiven.<br /><br />Some would ask, 'What does it matter? They're <em>characters</em>.' That's true. They are characters. But if I can't be fair in fiction, if I can't call out misogyny in my books, if I can't recognize rape-culture there....how can I effectively fight against these injustices in the real world? That's the question that occurred to me a few years ago. And now these things just pop out at me in books, tv, movies. Which isn't to say that I don't enjoy them anyway. Sometimes, even spotting the problematic elements, doesn't mean that I don't end up loving something. But seeing them, acknowledging them, calling them out - it's important to me now.<br /><br />This has become a review that has very little to do with this book and more to do with me. But because I've changed so much, and how I read books has changed so much, I went into this book worried. Even back then I was irritated with how Dorian treated Ashaya in the beginning of the book. His anger cuts through damn near everything, but he still pushes her romantically. Almost against his will, and with rage filtering through - it's a bunch of mixed signals that he gives Ashaya - and it's a bit of a personal sort spot for me.<br /><br />I worried that on this read, I would see Dorian's actions in a more glaring light - that he would become less the male that I loved throughout the series, and more someone I couldn't care about.<br /><br />Thankfully, that wasn't the case. Dorian <strong>is</strong> conflicted. He has a lot of rage in his soul, since losing his sister to a sociopathic member of the Psy race. To feel himself have feelings for a Psy, one who does everything in her power to maintain the Silence that he so hates....it's hard for him. He's not always nice, and he's quite often mean. I still don't like that. But it wasn't as bad as I was fearing. I understand why he acts the way he does. And what's better is that Ashaya doesn't stand and just meekly take it. She challenges him, expects respect, and demands that he deal with his issues.<br /><br />I like Ashaya a LOT more on this re-read. I know that I loved her before, but I love her even more now. She's as much a dominant as anyone in this series.<br /><br />The forward movement in the world, the fleshing out of the intricacies of relationships (on a large and small scale), is absolutely perfect. The overall story-arc is one of my favorite things about this series. It's so intricate and beautifully done, with enough tension and realism as to how things play out.<br /><br />I love this series. Going back through now, re-reading, is so much fun. All the more so because now, years later, I still love them as much as I did the first time.<br /><br />Review also available on <a href="https://thebookeaters.net/2016/09/02/review-hostage-to-pleasure/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Eaters</a><br /><br />Original Thoughts: Dorian was, from the first, a favorite character in this series. My heart broke for him in the first book (Slave to Sensation) seeing him directly after losing his sister to a monster. And each moment since then he has shown what a great person he is. Protective, loving, caring and loyal. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Well, until this book <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />It's his loyalty that gives him problems when he meets Ashaya Aleine - his mate. And a Psy. He fights himself, and his feelings for her, often to the point of cruelty to Ashaya. Mixed signals are all he's giving to her in the beginning and she doesn't know how to process them. <br /><br />Ashaya is another fascinating Psy. It's clear that her Silence isn't pure from the beginning. She obviously cares and is willing to go the distance for what she believes is right. Even if she justifies it to herself and others that it's for reasons that aren't emotional.<br /><br />Watching her struggle against her emotions was heart-breaking. She clearly felt, and yet there was a very real reason she couldn't show it. I was on the edge of my seat to figure out how this was going to work out. And in the end, I loved the resolution.<br /><br />Overall, a good book. 4 stars (1 star off for the cruelty from Dorian - I understood why he felt the way he felt, but it was just a too much for me).</span>
  <a data-text-id="18305554984193599295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1338136605" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1338136605" />
    <a title="Valerie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4148118-valerie"><img alt="Valerie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364076470p2/4148118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1338136605?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valerie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valerie" href="/user/show/4148118-valerie">Valerie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=re-reading">re-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=audio-reads">audio-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=own-copy">own-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=obsession">obsession</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1338136605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7906898511088615698">I continue to be amazed at how much I am enjoying this series. Each book completes a couple story but expands the overarching story of this world. And while the last book added the humans as featured characters, this one adds some human mystery. <br/><br/>Having never liked third person writing, I am equally amazed how much this authors third person writing just works for me. The POV changes and so the connections are made that I normally miss when reading this type of writing style. But because of this s</span>
  <span id="freeText7906898511088615698" style="display:none">I continue to be amazed at how much I am enjoying this series. Each book completes a couple story but expands the overarching story of this world. And while the last book added the humans as featured characters, this one adds some human mystery. <br /><br />Having never liked third person writing, I am equally amazed how much this authors third person writing just works for me. The POV changes and so the connections are made that I normally miss when reading this type of writing style. But because of this style, we learn so much about what's going on in with the Psy council and the mystery human group that pops up in this book.<br /><br />I love how this author adds the characters that will become important in the next book. This time, we learn a little bit more about Mercy and guess what? Her book is next. It's like when you need to know about them, they show up and that feature really appeals to me. <br /><br />Additionally, we get bits about couples that were previous featured. Lucas will always be around as the alpha of the cats but I love how we still see him take pleasure in kissing his mate and being there for pack. And I can't wait for more wolves. There was a bits and pieces with them in this book and so I love the dynamics over in the Snow Dancers pack. They have become good allies to the cats and vise versa. This makes me all kinds of happy. <br /><br />The writing continues to HOLD my attention, the story always surprises me and the characters are definitely part of my pack. I just can't get enough. More...give me more.<br /><br />AND did I mention HOT? These shifters love to touch. Love to bring the pleasure. Yum.<br /><br />Dorian. My heart broke for this cat that can't shift. He's become the best of the best just to prove his place as a Sentinel. His surfer looks and protective personality had me loving him even more. But this story was personal for this cat. How can he love someone from the race that killed his sister? He's vowed to take down the council. So he fought his cat on this one. Course, cats can be pretty persuasive. <br /><br />As for Ashaya...what a mystery this M-pys is. Nothing is as it seems. Even when I thought I had her figured out she had more secrets. Did I mention that Dorian doesn't like secrets? Some pretty fun scenes between these two as they tried to work through some of it. But nothing prepared me to love her as much as I did. Her love for her cat...her Dorian and how she completed him made her perfect to me. She doesn't back down from this protective cat. She loves him. She challenges him. She satisfies him. Yeah, I love her for that and all her little secrets.<br /><br />Satisfying. Addictive. Surprising. Enjoyable. Pleasurable. Demanding of my attention. AND it should be your next read...this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7906898511088615698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iwdC+YyEEqTLk+1LKJmri2vWFEXzRq6DePQGRGososHewYOHh30UYqiIPm6TR6ujsUNspwDEAoEZBzqH1nlJ8A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OsZ5HNzu932ZuzWDT6wz6Ud5SHODdiO+4c+ks94itIVvALhi1xfxu/qg5qb0cjPBnewwkXD0j7yAPJhwYndftA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer15550084412291166762">I've been writing as long as I can remember and all of my stories always held a thread of romance (even when I was writing about a prince who could shoot lasers out of his eyes). I love creating unique characters, love giving them happy endings and I even love the voices in my head. There's no other job I would rather be doing. In September 2002, when I got the call that Silhouette Desire wanted t</span>
  <span id="freeText15550084412291166762" style="display:none">I've been writing as long as I can remember and all of my stories always held a thread of romance (even when I was writing about a prince who could shoot lasers out of his eyes). I love creating unique characters, love giving them happy endings and I even love the voices in my head. There's no other job I would rather be doing. In September 2002, when I got the call that Silhouette Desire wanted to buy my first book, Desert Warrior, it was a dream come true. I hope to continue living the dream until I keel over of old age on my keyboard.<br /><br /><br />I was born in Fiji and raised in New Zealand. I also spent three years living and working in Japan, during which time I took the chance to travel around Asia. I’m back in New Zealand now, but I’m always plotting new trips. If you’d like to see some of my travel snapshots, have a look at the Travel Diary page (updated every month).<br /><br />So far, I've worked as a lawyer, a librarian, a candy factory general hand, a bank temp and an English teacher and not necessarily in that order. Some might call that inconsistency but I call it grist for the writer's mill.<br /><br /></span>

He sent you a present last week."<br /><br />Sascha smiled at the thought of Hawke's flirting. The SnowDancer alpha did it only to jerk Lucas's chain. "I never saw any present. What was it?"<br /><br />"How the hell should I know? I stomped on it and threw it into the deepest crevice I could find." He smirked. "Then I called him to ask how Sienna was doing."<br /><br />She burst out laughing. "Wicked, wicked man.&rdquo;</span>

What if you take the chance and you're wrong? What if you let yourself feel the loss and it's this huge pain and you can't put it back in the box?&rdquo;</span>
